Section 1:
ORR SUBSTITUTE TO HB238
OFFERED BY SENATOR ORR
1
2
3
4 SYNOPSIS: This bill makes appropriations for the
5 support, maintenance and development of public education in
6 Alabama, for debt service, and for capital outlay for
7 the fiscal year ending September 30, 2027.
8
9
10
11 A BILL
12 TO BE ENTITLED
13 AN ACT
14
15 To make appropriations for the support, maintenance and
16 development of public education in Alabama, for debt service,
17 and for capital outlay for the fiscal year ending September
18 30, 2027.
19 BE IT ENACTED BY THE LEGISLATURE OF ALABAMA:
20 Section 1. There is hereby appropriated for the support
21 of public education in Alabama for the fiscal year ending
22 September 30, 2027, for debt service, and for capital outlay
23 to be paid out of funds specified in subsection (a) of Section
24 2 of this act and the amounts specified in subsections (a),
25 (b), (c), (d), and (e) of Section 3 of this act. For the
26 purpose specified in subsection (b) of Section 2 of this act,
27 amounts are shown by programmatic area and the total for all
Page 1
amounts are shown by programmatic area and the total for all
RBPXJNM-1 04/01/2026 KHF (F) KHF SENATE FLOOR SUBSTITUTE TO
HB238
28 programs is shown so as to include estimated sources of funds
29 other than those listed in subsection (a) of Section 2 of this
30 act. For the purpose of this act, "ETF" shall mean the
31 Education Trust Fund and "Federal and Local Funds" shall mean
32 all gifts, grants, contributions, or entitlements, including
33 grants by the Congress of the United States, municipalities or
34 counties.
35 Section 2. (a) The appropriations provided for in this
36 act shall be paid from funds in the State Treasury to the
37 credit of the Education Trust Fund, Alabama Peace Officers'
38 Standards and Training Fund, Alabama Head and Spinal Cord
39 Injury Trust Fund, Driver Education and Training Fund, Special
40 Education Catastrophic Fund, Public School Fund and other
41 listed funds and are hereby made for the support of public
42 education in Alabama for the fiscal year ending September 30,
43 2027, and the appropriations herein made shall be subject to
44 the provisions, terms, conditions and limitations of the
45 Budget and Financial Control Act (Code of Alabama 1975,
46 Sections 41-4-80 et seq.), the provisions of the Budget
47 Management Act of 1976 (Code of Alabama 1975, Sections 41-19-1
48 et seq.), and shall be in the amounts hereinafter specified.
49 (b) Amounts shown hereinunder the columns "Other Funds"
50 and "Total" are as set forth for the purpose of establishing
51 amounts estimated to be available by programmatic area from
52 sources other than those listed in subsection (a) of this
53 Section 2, in order, upon consideration of such other funds so
54 estimated to be available, to promote the accountability for
Page 2
estimated to be available, to promote the accountability for
RBPXJNM-1 04/01/2026 KHF (F) KHF SENATE FLOOR SUBSTITUTE TO
HB238
55 an efficient use of funds available, and the same are hereby
56 appropriated by the Legislature. Provided, however, that
57 regardless of the ending date of any pay period which has been
58 or may be established by the Legislature for the payment of
59 salaries of state employees, the entire payment due shall be
60 made from the fiscal year's appropriation in which the pay
61 date falls.
62 (c) All appropriations made in Section 3 shall be at
63 the program level. Any directed expenditure of funds below a
64 program shall be from funds appropriated for the program.
Page 3
program shall be from funds appropriated for the program.

133 The Council on the Arts may award grants from the facilities grant program for projects that
134 build, renovate, restore, preserve, or enhance arts facilities in Alabama, including performing
135 arts centers, art museums and galleries, multi-purpose arts centers, artist residency
136 facilities, and outdoor performance venues. The Council on the Arts shall emphasize rural
137 assistance with grants, with a preference for entities not receiving grants in the prior year.
138 Eligible entities include: (i) 501(c) (3) nonprofit arts organizations chartered in Alabama,
139 active and in good standing with the Internal Revenue Service and the council; or (ii) an
140 entity of local government. Grant amounts shall not exceed $100,000 to any one entity, with the
141 first two grants being reserved for the Arts Council of the Trussville Area Theater for $75,000
142 and the Carnegie Visual Arts Center for $100,000.

Education
Trust Fund Other Funds Total
185 The funds appropriated for Workforce Development are to be expended for those costs
186 incurred by the State in honoring commitments to pay workforce development costs,
187 including services and other assistance and expenses of recruitment and training of
188 a company's workforce, that are undertaken to induce companies to locate and expand
189 their operations in Alabama (described hereinafter as a "Project") and to develop
190 and implement training, placement and recruitment programs that will improve
191 development and expand the State's workforce. Such costs include, but are not
192 limited to: (i) AIDT operating costs directly related to a Project; (ii) wages and
193 benefits for trainers engaged by AIDT for the purpose of a Project; (iii) costs
194 which the State has agreed to pay under the terms of a Project Agreement with a
195 company that are necessary and reasonable charges incurred by the company or its
196 affiliates for personnel providing training to the company's employees, whether
197 those trainers are employees of the company or its vendors or suppliers, including
198 wages, benefits and travel (domestic and, when necessary, international); (iv) any
199 necessary materials, equipment, manuals, or other relevant training materials; (v)
200 the costs incurred for purchasing or repairing or replacing training tools and
201 equipment; (vi) costs incurred for the purchase or construction and maintenance of
202 training facilities; (vii) travel expenses for prospective and current employees and
203 trainees, including travel, food, lodging, relocation, and other costs necessary and
204 reasonable to enable the company to secure a qualified workforce; and (viii) outside
205 training fees. The above funds appropriated for Workforce Development shall be
206 expended primarily for the training of Alabama residents. It is further the intent
207 that contracts with vendors to provide workforce training shall be inclusive and
208 reflect the racial and gender diversity of the State. The Secretary of the
209 Department of Commerce shall report semi-annually to the Chairs of the Senate
210 Committee on Finance and Taxation-Education, the House Ways and Means-Education
211 Committee, the Finance Director, and the Legislative Fiscal Officer any funds
212 allocated for workforce training. Such report shall include a summary of the persons
213 trained and the vendors providing the training. The report shall contain information
214 including the residence, race and gender of the persons trained and of the principal
215 or majority owner of the firm or business contracted with to provide the training
216 services.
Page 8
services.

347 Pursuant to Sections 22-18-60, et seq., Code of Alabama 1975.
348 (q) Automotive Workforce Training 400,000 400,000
349 Scholarship Program
350 The Board of Trustees of the Alabama Community College System, in consultation
351 with the Alabama Industrial Development and Training Institute, shall
352 establish qualifications for the award of scholarships to high school students
353 and adults enrolled in a state educational program relating to the automotive
354 manufacturing industry and shall further provide for the implementation and
355 administration of the scholarships. Scholarship recipients shall be selected
356 by the Board, in consultation with a scholarship committee, comprised of
357 members of the Board of Directors of the Alabama Automotive Manufacturers
358 Association, from applications submitted to the association. The Board shall
359 file a report with the Chairs of the Senate Committee on Finance and
360 Taxation-Education, the House Ways and Means-Education Committee, the
361 Legislative Fiscal Officer, and the Finance Director on September 30, 2027
362 regarding the total number of scholarships awarded for the Fall term of the
363 2026-2027 academic year and the institution attended by the scholarship
364 recipients. The report shall also include the name of each scholarship
365 recipient and the number of years the recipient has received a scholarship.

600,000
(CALT) Stipend Program
RBPXJNM-1 04/01/2026 KHF (F) KHF SENATE FLOOR SUBSTITUTE TO HB238
Education
Trust Fund Other Funds Total
1010 The above appropriation includes funds to pay salary supplements and related benefit costs for
1011 Certified Academic Language Therapists (CALT) and other costs of the program. Supplement
1012 amounts will be determined by the availability of funds based on the number of CALT
1013 Teachers. The state of Alabama will provide an annual supplement of $5,000 to any CALT that is
1014 employed full-time in a public K-12 school system or public independent school and is properly
1015 certified by the state of Alabama. The existing eligibility criteria will apply: (a) CALTs
1016 employed on less than a full-time contract on October 1 will receive a pro-rata share of the
1017 salary supplement. (b) CALTs employed full-time after October 1 will receive a pro-rata share
1018 of the salary supplement. (c) Any CALT employed full-time in Alabama and properly certified by
1019 the state of Alabama will receive the annual salary stipend. (d) CALTs employed as a substitute
1020 are not eligible for the salary supplement. (e) CALTs who are on leave of absence for more than
1021 half a school year will receive a prorated amount based on the number of months worked during
1022 the school year. (f) CALTs will receive the salary supplement each year of the valid period of
1023 the CALT credentials unless the Alabama Legislature declines to make the annual appropriation.
1024 (g) CALTs must maintain their CALT credentials in order to continue receiving the salary
1025 supplement. (h) CALTs employed in the final year of their CALT credentials valid period will
1026 receive a prorated amount based on the number of months worked covered in that valid period.
1027 (i) CALTs who leave after October 1 will be eligible for a prorated amount based on the months
1028 served. (j) CALTs must remain employed with a public K-12 Local Board of Education school
1029 system or public independent school to continue receiving the salary supplement.

1032 Of the above appropriation, $17,200,000 shall be expended for the Alabama Summer and
1033 Afterschool Program (ASAP) grants program with the objective of reducing the achievement gap in
1034 students who are not proficient in reading and/or math.
1035 The State Superintendent of Education shall administer the grants process. Grants shall be
1036 awarded to a) local education agencies, municipalities, and not-for-profit organizations for
1037 summer and afterschool programs that provide direct services and b) to entities that provide
1038 support to summer and after-school programs. Afterschool programs shall be guided by the
1039 Alabama Afterschool Quality Standards; summer programs shall be guided by the "Final Report and
1040 Recommendations" of the Alabama Campaign for Grade-Level Reading, Pages 81-92.
1041 Data on student and program outcomes shall be collected and used to inform a continuous
1042 improvement process. A report shall be provided to the Legislature listing grantees and
1043 summarizing outcomes.
1044 The intent of the Legislature is to increase access to evidence-based, high-quality summer and
1045 afterschool programming, to build a diverse delivery model of providers, and to foster
1046 collaboration between local education agencies and community-based organizations. The goal is
1047 to award at least 60% of the funding to nonprofit, community based organizations or
1048 partnerships between community-based organizations and local education agencies.

1144 To be expended for the Bullying Prevention Project in accordance with Title 16, Chapter 28B,
1145 Code of Alabama 1975. The State Superintendent of Education shall distribute the above
1146 appropriation as grants to local education agencies. These agencies may be awarded funds only
1147 after application to the State Department of Education. The grant application process may
1148 require the submission of plans by the applicant to meet the requirements set forth in Chapter
1149 28B of Title 16. In the awarding of grants, preference will be given to applicants seeking to
1150 develop and implement evidence-based practices to promote a school environment that is free of
1151 harassment, intimidation, violence, and threats of violence. This program may also address tier
1152 one and tier two of the school-based mental health model of all students receiving prevention
1153 education and peers working to support and identify at-risk students. Additionally, the program
1154 may focus to increase school safety through early identification of at-risk students,
1155 minimizing disciplinary infractions including school suspensions and expulsions. The program
1156 may provide grade level prevention curriculum for all students and, in that case, the
1157 curriculum must be updated annually to remain current and relevant to current trends that youth
1158 face in their lives. Any applicable prevention curriculum must be comprehensive and satisfy the
1159 following state mandates: Erin's Law, Jamari Terrell Williams Student Bullying Prevention Act,
1160 Jason Flatt Act, Price Hornsby Act, and drugs and alcohol prevention programs. In addition, any
1161 program related to mental health should be flexible enough to focus on the greatest mental
1162 health needs for each individual school. For accountability purposes, reporting data must
1163 include the number of students engaged in the programs, the number of students supported, and
1164 the number of students referred to adults as at-risk.

1194 This appropriation shall be used for the State Department of Education, in consultation with
1195 the Department of Early Childhood Education, to fund a program to be known as the Governor's
1196 Turnaround Schools. These grants are for the lowest performing public elementary schools which
1197 are identified as underperforming by the State Superintendent in consideration of the
1198 provisions of the Alabama Accountability Act, the State Report Card System, and other criteria
1199 as determined by the State Superintendent. The intent of these grants is to identify and target
1200 specific deficiencies of each individual underperforming elementary school and target said
1201 deficiencies with high quality and innovative educational supports. In consultation with these
1202 schools as well as the local education agencies that respectively oversee these schools, the
1203 State Department of Education will develop and oversee a comprehensive plan for school
1204 improvement. It is the intention of this provision that all areas of the State Department,
1205 including Alabama Reading Initiative, Alabama Math, Science, and Technology Initiative, Office
1206 of Mathematics Improvement, and Office of School Improvement, will work together to best serve
1207 these selected schools. Schools previously named to this list will be known as Cohort 1.
1208 Beginning with the fiscal year 2027 Budget Request, the State Department will recommend a
1209 pathway for schools in Cohort 1 to exit this program, and the Department will recommend new
1210 schools to replace those exiting the program in subsequent years. These schools may be known as
1211 Cohort 2 and so forth. The State Superintendent may also request additional funds so that
1212 additional cohorts can be expanded as Cohort 1 schools leave the program over the next few
1213 years. Any expansion of new Cohorts should be modest with respect to the purpose of this
1214 program which is expected to offer extraordinary supports to a relatively limited number of
1215 schools at a time. The State Department of Education should annually produce written progress
1216 reports on these schools to the Chair of the House Ways and Means - Education Committee, the
1217
Chair of the Senate Finance and Taxation - Education Committee, the Governor, and the Local
1218
School Board, Superintendent, and Principal of each school.

1395 The above appropriation includes funds to pay salary supplements and related benefit costs for
1396 Nationally Board-Certified Teachers (NBCT) and other costs of the program. Supplement amounts
1397 will be determined by the availability of funds based on the number of National Board Certified
1398 Teachers. (1) The state of Alabama will provide an annual supplement of $5,000 to any NBCT that
1399 is employed full-time in a public K-12 school and is properly certified by the state of
1400 Alabama. The existing eligibility criteria will apply: (a) NBCTs employed on a less than
1401 full-time contract on October 1 will receive a pro-rata share of the salary supplement. (b)
1402 NBCTs employed full-time after October 1 will receive a pro-rata share of the salary
1403 supplement. (c) NBCTs who earn National Board Certification in another state and are teaching
1404 full-time in Alabama on October 1 and are properly certified by the state of Alabama will
1405 receive the annual salary stipend. (d) NBCTs employed as a substitute are not eligible for the
1406 salary supplement. (e) NBCTs who are on leave of absence for more than half a school year will
1407 receive a prorated amount based on the number of months worked during the school year. (f)
1408 NBCTs will receive the salary supplement each year of the valid period of the certificate
1409 unless the Alabama Legislature declines to make the annual appropriation. (g) NBCTs must renew
1410 their certificate by the year of the certificate's expiration in order to continue receiving
1411 the salary supplement. (h) NBCTs employed in the final year of the certificate valid period
1412 will receive a prorated amount based on the number of months worked covered in that valid
1413 period. (i) NBCTs who leave after October 1 will be eligible for a prorated amount based on the
1414 months served. (j) NBCTs must remain employed with a public K-12 local Board of Education in
1415 order to continue receiving the salary supplement. (2) In addition to the supplement provided
1416 by subsection (1) of this section, classroom teachers shall be eligible for an additional
1417 supplement of $5,000 if in an instructional assignment in challenging, high poverty schools,
1418
subject to the following conditions and limitations: (a) Teacher holds a valid NBPTS
1419
certificate in Literacy, English Language Arts, English as a New Language, Math, Science,
1420
Exceptional Needs, or Career and Technical Education; and (b) School has been on the "Priority
1421
School" list 3 of the last 5 years; and/or (c) School has a graduation rate more than 10% less
1422
than the state average for 2 of the 3 most recently posted years; and/or (d) School has a free

133 The Council on the Arts may award grants from the facilities grant program for projects that
134 build, renovate, restore, preserve, or enhance arts facilities in Alabama, including performing
135 arts centers, art museums and galleries, multi-purpose arts centers, artist residency
136 facilities, and outdoor performance venues. The Council on the Arts shall emphasize rural
137 assistance with grants, with a preference for entities not receiving grants in the prior year.
138 Eligible entities include: (i) 501(c) (3) nonprofit arts organizations chartered in Alabama,

140 entity of local government. Grant amounts shall not exceed $100,000 to any one entity, with the
141 first two grants being reserved for the Arts Council of the Trussville Area Theater for $75,000

185 The funds appropriated for Workforce Development are to be expended for those costs
186 incurred by the State in honoring commitments to pay workforce development costs,
187 including services and other assistance and expenses of recruitment and training of
188 a company's workforce, that are undertaken to induce companies to locate and expand
189 their operations in Alabama (described hereinafter as a "Project") and to develop
190 and implement training, placement and recruitment programs that will improve
191 development and expand the State's workforce. Such costs include, but are not
192 limited to: (i) AIDT operating costs directly related to a Project; (ii) wages and
193 benefits for trainers engaged by AIDT for the purpose of a Project; (iii) costs
194 which the State has agreed to pay under the terms of a Project Agreement with a
195 company that are necessary and reasonable charges incurred by the company or its
196 affiliates for personnel providing training to the company's employees, whether
197 those trainers are employees of the company or its vendors or suppliers, including
198 wages, benefits and travel (domestic and, when necessary, international); (iv) any
199 necessary materials, equipment, manuals, or other relevant training materials; (v)
200 the costs incurred for purchasing or repairing or replacing training tools and
201 equipment; (vi) costs incurred for the purchase or construction and maintenance of
202 training facilities; (vii) travel expenses for prospective and current employees and
203 trainees, including travel, food, lodging, relocation, and other costs necessary and
204 reasonable to enable the company to secure a qualified workforce; and (viii) outside
205 training fees. The above funds appropriated for Workforce Development shall be
206 expended primarily for the training of Alabama residents. It is further the intent
207 that contracts with vendors to provide workforce training shall be inclusive and
208 reflect the racial and gender diversity of the State. The Secretary of the
209 Department of Commerce shall report semi-annually to the Chairs of the Senate
210 Committee on Finance and Taxation-Education, the House Ways and Means-Education
211 Committee, the Finance Director, and the Legislative Fiscal Officer any funds
212 allocated for workforce training. Such report shall include a summary of the persons
213 trained and the vendors providing the training. The report shall contain information
214 including the residence, race and gender of the persons trained and of the principal
215 or majority owner of the firm or business contracted with to provide the training
216 services.

1010 The above appropriation includes funds to pay salary supplements and related benefit costs for
1011 Certified Academic Language Therapists (CALT) and other costs of the program. Supplement
1012 amounts will be determined by the availability of funds based on the number of CALT
1013 Teachers. The state of Alabama will provide an annual supplement of $5,000 to any CALT that is
1014 employed full-time in a public K-12 school system or public independent school and is properly
1015 certified by the state of Alabama. The existing eligibility criteria will apply: (a) CALTs
1016 employed on less than a full-time contract on October 1 will receive a pro-rata share of the
1017 salary supplement. (b) CALTs employed full-time after October 1 will receive a pro-rata share
1018 of the salary supplement. (c) Any CALT employed full-time in Alabama and properly certified by
1019 the state of Alabama will receive the annual salary stipend. (d) CALTs employed as a substitute
1020 are not eligible for the salary supplement. (e) CALTs who are on leave of absence for more than
1021 half a school year will receive a prorated amount based on the number of months worked during
1022 the school year. (f) CALTs will receive the salary supplement each year of the valid period of
1023 the CALT credentials unless the Alabama Legislature declines to make the annual appropriation.
1024 (g) CALTs must maintain their CALT credentials in order to continue receiving the salary
1025 supplement. (h) CALTs employed in the final year of their CALT credentials valid period will
1026 receive a prorated amount based on the number of months worked covered in that valid period.
1027 (i) CALTs who leave after October 1 will be eligible for a prorated amount based on the months
1028 served. (j) CALTs must remain employed with a public K-12 Local Board of Education school
1029 system or public independent school to continue receiving the salary supplement.

1032 Of the above appropriation, $17,200,000 shall be expended for the Alabama Summer and
1033 Afterschool Program (ASAP) grants program with the objective of reducing the achievement gap in
1034 students who are not proficient in reading and/or math.
1035 The State Superintendent of Education shall administer the grants process. Grants shall be
1036 awarded to a) local education agencies, municipalities, and not-for-profit organizations for
1037 summer and afterschool programs that provide direct services and b) to entities that provide
1038 support to summer and after-school programs. Afterschool programs shall be guided by the
1039 Alabama Afterschool Quality Standards; summer programs shall be guided by the "Final Report and
1040 Recommendations" of the Alabama Campaign for Grade-Level Reading, Pages 81-92.
1041 Data on student and program outcomes shall be collected and used to inform a continuous
1042 improvement process. A report shall be provided to the Legislature listing grantees and
1043 summarizing outcomes.
1044 The intent of the Legislature is to increase access to evidence-based, high-quality summer and
1045 afterschool programming, to build a diverse delivery model of providers, and to foster
1046 collaboration between local education agencies and community-based organizations. The goal is
1047 to award at least 60% of the funding to nonprofit, community based organizations or
1048 partnerships between community-based organizations and local education agencies.

1144 To be expended for the Bullying Prevention Project in accordance with Title 16, Chapter 28B,
1145 Code of Alabama 1975. The State Superintendent of Education shall distribute the above
1146 appropriation as grants to local education agencies. These agencies may be awarded funds only
1147 after application to the State Department of Education. The grant application process may
1148 require the submission of plans by the applicant to meet the requirements set forth in Chapter
1149 28B of Title 16. In the awarding of grants, preference will be given to applicants seeking to
1150 develop and implement evidence-based practices to promote a school environment that is free of
1151 harassment, intimidation, violence, and threats of violence. This program may also address tier
1152 one and tier two of the school-based mental health model of all students receiving prevention
1153 education and peers working to support and identify at-risk students. Additionally, the program
1154 may focus to increase school safety through early identification of at-risk students,
1155 minimizing disciplinary infractions including school suspensions and expulsions. The program
1156 may provide grade level prevention curriculum for all students and, in that case, the
1157 curriculum must be updated annually to remain current and relevant to current trends that youth
1158 face in their lives. Any applicable prevention curriculum must be comprehensive and satisfy the
1159 following state mandates: Erin's Law, Jamari Terrell Williams Student Bullying Prevention Act,
1160 Jason Flatt Act, Price Hornsby Act, and drugs and alcohol prevention programs. In addition, any
1161 program related to mental health should be flexible enough to focus on the greatest mental
1162 health needs for each individual school. For accountability purposes, reporting data must
1163 include the number of students engaged in the programs, the number of students supported, and
1164 the number of students referred to adults as at-risk.

1194 This appropriation shall be used for the State Department of Education, in consultation with
1195 the Department of Early Childhood Education, to fund a program to be known as the Governor's
1196 Turnaround Schools. These grants are for the lowest performing public elementary schools which
1197 are identified as underperforming by the State Superintendent in consideration of the
1198 provisions of the Alabama Accountability Act, the State Report Card System, and other criteria
1199 as determined by the State Superintendent. The intent of these grants is to identify and target
1200 specific deficiencies of each individual underperforming elementary school and target said
1201 deficiencies with high quality and innovative educational supports. In consultation with these
1202 schools as well as the local education agencies that respectively oversee these schools, the
1203 State Department of Education will develop and oversee a comprehensive plan for school
1204 improvement. It is the intention of this provision that all areas of the State Department,
1205 including Alabama Reading Initiative, Alabama Math, Science, and Technology Initiative, Office
1206 of Mathematics Improvement, and Office of School Improvement, will work together to best serve
1207 these selected schools. Schools previously named to this list will be known as Cohort 1.
1208 Beginning with the fiscal year 2027 Budget Request, the State Department will recommend a
1209 pathway for schools in Cohort 1 to exit this program, and the Department will recommend new
1210 schools to replace those exiting the program in subsequent years. These schools may be known as
1211 Cohort 2 and so forth. The State Superintendent may also request additional funds so that
1212 additional cohorts can be expanded as Cohort 1 schools leave the program over the next few
1213 years. Any expansion of new Cohorts should be modest with respect to the purpose of this
1214 program which is expected to offer extraordinary supports to a relatively limited number of
1215 schools at a time. The State Department of Education should annually produce written progress
1216 reports on these schools to the Chair of the House Ways and Means - Education Committee, the
1217
Chair of the Senate Finance and Taxation - Education Committee, the Governor, and the Local
1218
School Board, Superintendent, and Principal of each school.

1395 The above appropriation includes funds to pay salary supplements and related benefit costs for
1396 Nationally Board-Certified Teachers (NBCT) and other costs of the program. Supplement amounts
1397 will be determined by the availability of funds based on the number of National Board Certified
1398 Teachers. (1) The state of Alabama will provide an annual supplement of $5,000 to any NBCT that
1399 is employed full-time in a public K-12 school and is properly certified by the state of
1400 Alabama. The existing eligibility criteria will apply: (a) NBCTs employed on a less than
1401 full-time contract on October 1 will receive a pro-rata share of the salary supplement. (b)
1402 NBCTs employed full-time after October 1 will receive a pro-rata share of the salary
1403 supplement. (c) NBCTs who earn National Board Certification in another state and are teaching
1404 full-time in Alabama on October 1 and are properly certified by the state of Alabama will
1405 receive the annual salary stipend. (d) NBCTs employed as a substitute are not eligible for the
1406 salary supplement. (e) NBCTs who are on leave of absence for more than half a school year will
1407 receive a prorated amount based on the number of months worked during the school year. (f)
1408 NBCTs will receive the salary supplement each year of the valid period of the certificate
1409 unless the Alabama Legislature declines to make the annual appropriation. (g) NBCTs must renew
1410 their certificate by the year of the certificate's expiration in order to continue receiving
1411 the salary supplement. (h) NBCTs employed in the final year of the certificate valid period
1412 will receive a prorated amount based on the number of months worked covered in that valid
1413 period. (i) NBCTs who leave after October 1 will be eligible for a prorated amount based on the
1414 months served. (j) NBCTs must remain employed with a public K-12 local Board of Education in
1415 order to continue receiving the salary supplement. (2) In addition to the supplement provided
1416 by subsection (1) of this section, classroom teachers shall be eligible for an additional
1417 supplement of $5,000 if in an instructional assignment in challenging, high poverty schools,
1418
subject to the following conditions and limitations: (a) Teacher holds a valid NBPTS
1419
certificate in Literacy, English Language Arts, English as a New Language, Math, Science,
1420
Exceptional Needs, or Career and Technical Education; and (b) School has been on the "Priority
1421

(1) Operating Grant Program 4,000,000

1864 To be distributed as grants to monuments to commemorate historical events and places,
1865 historical skills centers, cultural heritage parks, historic sites, commissions, boards,
1866 agencies, and authorities that are not owned, operated, or otherwise under the control of the
1867 Alabama Historical Commission or other state agencies. Grants will be awarded to entities that
1868 reflect a historical education-based mission and concentrate on historical educational
1869 programming. Preference shall be given to: (1) any property constructed prior to 1840 that is
1870 listed in or eligible for the National Register of Historic Places and that are publicly owned
1871 and accessible to the public; or (2) any property in Alabama built in 1943 or before, and is
1872 listed in or eligible for the National Register of Historic Places or any property built after
1873 1943 that significantly contributed to the civil rights movement. The first three grants shall
1874 be reserved for Old State Bank for $200,000, Hartselle Historical Depot for $100,000, and Mt.
1875 Pinson Presbyterian Church for $75,000. Remaining grant amounts shall not exceed $100,000 for

2844 Section 21. Colleges and universities which receive
2845 Education Trust Fund appropriations shall not set
2846 per-credit-hour tuition rates for dual enrollment or early
2847 college courses below the per-credit-hour tuition rate of the
2848 Alabama Community College System institutions as adopted by

2849 the ACCS Board of Trustees annually. The Alabama Commission on
2850 Higher Education shall publish each college and university's
2851 dual enrollment tuition rates annually on their website and
2852 provide guidance to institutions to ensure compliance with
2853 this section.
2854 Section 22. Notwithstanding any other provision of law
2855 to the contrary, out of any excess revenues remaining in the
2856 Education Trust Fund from Fiscal Year 2026 that become
2857 nonrecurring revenue available for supplemental appropriation
2858 in Fiscal Year 2027 pursuant to subdivision (4) of Section
2859 29-9-4, Code of Alabama 1975, there is hereby appropriated a
2860 total of $32,900,000 from the Education Trust Fund to the
2861 Teachers' Retirement System for a one-time longevity bonus for
2862 retirees of the Teachers' Retirement System. The funds
